</th>

<p><b>Malaysia national football team</b> (<a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>: <span lang="ms" xml:lang="ms"><i><b>Pasukan bola sepak kebangsaan Malaysia</b></i></span>) is the national team of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">Football Association of Malaysia</a> (FAM). The national team was founded in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merdeka_Tournament" title="Merdeka Tournament">1963 Merdeka Tournament</a> one month before the establishment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaysian_Federation" title="Malaysian Federation">Malaysian Federation</a>. Malaysia national football team is recognised by FIFA as the successor of the defunct <a href="/wiki/Malaya_national_football_team" title="Malaya national football team">Malaya national football team</a>. The Malaysian team nicknamed <i>Harimau Malaysia</i> (formerly nicknamed <i>Harimau Malaya</i>, in reference of the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_tiger" title="Malayan tiger">Malayan tiger</a>).</p>
<p>It is one of the successful teams in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_national_football_team" title="Indonesia national football team">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_national_football_team" title="Singapore national football team">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_national_football_team" title="Vietnam national football team">Vietnam</a>, winning bronze at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Asian_Games" title="Football at the Asian Games">Asian Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1974_Asian_Games" title="Football at the 1974 Asian Games">1974</a> as well winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN_Football_Championship" title="ASEAN Football Championship">ASEAN Football Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship" title="2010 AFF Championship">2010</a> and other small competitions while improving at the same time.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>, Malaysia's highest standing was in the first release of the figures, in August 1993, at 75th. Malaysia's main rival on the international stage are their geographical neighbours, Indonesia and Singapore, and past matches between these two teams have produced much drama.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i>Harimau Malaya</i> name have been inherited from the <a href="/wiki/Malaya_national_football_team" title="Malaya national football team">Malaya national football team</a> (which derived from <i><a href="/wiki/Malayan_tiger" title="Malayan tiger">Malayan tiger</a></i>). Although the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaysia" title="Federation of Malaysia">Federation of Malaysia</a> have been formed in 16 September 1963, the name are still being maintained for the national squad, thus there is some debate as most Malaysian in the <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East</a> felt the <i>"<a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Malaya</a>"</i> term does not cover the whole country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> Another source stated the name was believed to have been derived from a Malayan football player from Stulang Laut, <a href="/wiki/Johor" title="Johor">Johor</a> named <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Abdullah_Mohd_Don&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Abdullah Mohd Don (page does not exist)">Abdullah Mohd Don</a> (Dollah Don)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> after he been called as "Harimau Malaya" by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">founding father of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> when managed to chasing his team lost of 0–3 against an Indonesian football club by scoring <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> in a match between Singaporean Malay Club and Peseja (<a href="/wiki/Persija_Jakarta" title="Persija Jakarta">Persija Jakarta</a>) in 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> On 2 February 2016, the nickname was officially changed to <i>Harimau Malaysia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inclusive_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-inclusive-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_debate_and_official_change">Naming debate and official change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Naming debate and official change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most supporters in the East felt offended when the media in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Malaysia" title="West Malaysia">West Malaysia</a> keep continuously using the term even some in the West said it is just a small matter and the naming issue had been politicised, but for the people in the East it contradicts the aspirations and the spirit of <a href="/wiki/1Malaysia" title="1Malaysia">1Malaysia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> Most also has upset and disappointed as if the national team lose, the team will started to be called as <i>Malaysian tiger</i>, but if the national team won they will be only called as <i>Malayan tiger</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hm_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-hm-11">[10]</a></sup> Thus from 2 February 2016 onward, the nickname <i>Harimau Malaya</i> was officially changed to <i>Harimau Malaysia</i> in a bid to be more inclusive especially to the East Malaysian sides. The <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">Football Association of Malaysia</a> (FAM) president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tengku_Abdullah_Sultan_Ahmad_Shah" title="Tengku Abdullah Sultan Ahmad Shah">Tengku Abdullah</a> said in a statement that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inclusive_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-inclusive-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">FAM feels Harimau Malaya is no longer suitable in view of the fact the word Malaya itself is not used widely in the country after the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Agreement" title="Malaysia Agreement">formation of Malaysia in 1963</a>. I hope the new name better reflects that the national team belongs to all Malaysians. But I don't want just a name change, the players must have a new spirit to seek success...a Harimau Malaysia which is more fearsome and can devour its opponents, at least in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inclusive_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-inclusive-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_foundation">Early foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Malaya_national_football_team" title="Malaya national football team">Malaya national football team</a></div>
<p>Before the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> on 16 September 1963, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Malaya</a> and Singapore are represented by their own national teams, a situation which pre-dated the establishment of a Malaysia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> Malaya and Singapore usually competed in an international competition such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merdeka_Tournament" title="Merdeka Tournament">Merdeka Tournament</a> while <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Sarawak</a> competed in <a href="/wiki/Borneo_Cup" title="Borneo Cup">Borneo Cup</a>. <a href="/wiki/Malaya_national_football_team" title="Malaya national football team">Malaya</a>'s biggest achievement in football was becoming the bronze medalist of the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1962_Asian_Games" title="Football at the 1962 Asian Games">1962 Asian Games</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Indonesia after defeating <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam_national_football_team" title="South Vietnam national football team">South Vietnam</a> 4–1.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner,_North_Borneo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="762" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg/220px-1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg/330px-1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg/440px-1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner%2C_North_Borneo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1962_Borneo_Cup_Winner,_North_Borneo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The winner of the first season of <a href="/wiki/Borneo_Cup" title="Borneo Cup">Borneo Cup</a> in 1962, <a href="/wiki/Sabah_FA" title="Sabah FA">North Borneo</a> football team, one year before the merger to form Malaysia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The beginning of Malaysia football team match took place in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merdeka_Stadium" title="Merdeka Stadium">Merdeka Stadium</a> on 8 August 1963 with the combined strength of Singapore and Malaya (although the federation was only existed after 16 September 1963). With the combined forces of Malaya and Singapore, the team start their match with <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>, thought lost 3–4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> The team continued to use combination of players from Singapore and <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> until the formation of the Malaysian Federation and ended when <a href="/wiki/Singapore_in_Malaysia" title="Singapore in Malaysia">Singapore's separated from Malaysia</a> in 1965. Since then the squad was only represented by West Malaysian players, mainly due to difficulties of that time to travel to <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East Malaysia</a> and the players were not well known to mainstream West Malaysian football. It was only in 1977; when the FAM sent a talent scout to the East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> In 1971, <a href="/wiki/James_Wong_(footballer)" title="James Wong (footballer)">James Wong</a> of Sabah is the first player from East Malaysia to represent the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> The list continued by the late <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=James_Yaakub&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="James Yaakub (page does not exist)">James Yaakub</a> of <a href="/wiki/Former_Sarawak_FA_players" title="Former Sarawak FA players">Sarawak</a> in 1977.</p>
<p>Malaysia qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1972_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei_national_football_team" title="Chinese Taipei national football team">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philippines_national_football_team" title="Philippines national football team">Philippines</a> along the way. Although they managed to defeat the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a> 3–0, they lost the other 2 matches with a score of 3–0 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Germany_national_football_team" title="West Germany national football team">West Germany</a> and 6–0 to <a href="/wiki/Morocco_national_football_team" title="Morocco national football team">Morocco</a>. Two years later, Malaysia won their second bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/1974_Asian_Games" title="1974 Asian Games">1974 Asian Games</a> after defeating <a href="/wiki/North_Korea_national_football_team" title="North Korea national football team">North Korea</a> 2–1. The team went on to qualify twice in a row for the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a>, in 1976 and 1980. Malaysia qualified again for the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Olympics</a> in Moscow, but joined the boycott of the games. The team also won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merdeka_Tournament" title="Merdeka Tournament">Merdeka Tournament</a> three times, became runner-up four times and achieved third place twice during the 1970s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1972.E2.80.931985_and_records">1972–1985 and records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1972–1985 and records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1972, <a href="/wiki/Mokhtar_Dahari" title="Mokhtar Dahari">Mokhtar Dahari</a> is considered as the legend footballer for the Malaysian team as he booked his place as one of the best players in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-md_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-md-3">[3]</a></sup> He manage to score 175 goals, of which the 175 goals for <a href="/wiki/Selangor_FA" title="Selangor FA">Selangor FA</a>, 20 goals in 13 appearances for Kwong Yik Bank and another 125 goals for the national team, giving a total of 320 goals in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asian Football Confederation</a> (AFC) and <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_%26_Statistics" title="International Federation of Football History &amp; Statistics">IFFHS</a> denied the result as there is no evidence for the claim, and said the player only scored 5 goals in 20 matches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The FIFA also said "the highest record for the Malaysian team is only having score approximately 110 goals in international matches from 1972 until 1985, but it is still not possible for the player to score 175 goals".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Therefore, Mokhtar Dahari is not recognised by FIFA to be the top scorer in Asian football.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1994.E2.80.932011">1994–2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1994–2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1994, Malaysian football was embroiled in one of the largest bribery scandals in the country. With the dearth of mainstream interest and lack of funds, Malaysian football has failed to repeat the achievements of the 1970s and 1980s, despite the recruitment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claude_LeRoy" title="Claude LeRoy">Claude LeRoy</a>. Harris came with strong credentials, having assisted <a href="/wiki/Terry_Venables" title="Terry Venables">Terry Venables</a> at <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allan_Harris" title="Allan Harris">Allan Harris</a> as coaches.</p>
<p>In the second half of 2004, <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">FAM</a> selected <a href="/wiki/Bertalan_Bicskei" title="Bertalan Bicskei">Bertalan Bicskei</a>, former Hungarian goalkeeper and national coach, to succeed Allan Harris. Bicskei led the national side to third place at the regional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiger_Cup" title="Tiger Cup">Tiger Cup</a> tournament, but was demoted to youth development duties by FAM for his actions during a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Singapore_national_football_team" title="Singapore national football team">Singapore</a> in <a href="/wiki/Penang" title="Penang">Penang</a> on 8 June 2005. Bicskei, disgusted by the standard of officiating, threw a bottle onto the pitch before confronting a Singapore player. In September 2005, his contract was terminated after a mutual agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norizan_Bakar" title="Norizan Bakar">Norizan Bakar</a> became the next head coach of the Malaysian team. He guided the Malaysian squad to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_ASEAN_Football_Championship" title="2007 ASEAN Football Championship">ASEAN Cup</a> semifinals in 2007, where Malaysia lost through penalties to Singapore. Norizan's position as the head coach was criticised by the Malaysian football community, fans and officials alike, after the team's performances during the <a href="/wiki/2007_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2007 AFC Asian Cup">2007 AFC Asian Cup</a>, where Malaysia lost to China 1–5, Uzbekistan 0–5 and Iran 0–2.</p>
<p>After the removal of Norizan Bakar, B. Sathianathan took over as head coach. Although he guided the squad to win the <a href="/wiki/2007_Merdeka_Tournament" title="2007 Merdeka Tournament">2007 Merdeka Tournament</a>, Malaysia once again failed to qualify for the World Cup after losing 4–1 and drawing 0–0 with Bahrain in the qualifying round. In March 2008, Sathianathan once again reach the final of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Merdeka_Tournament" title="2008 Merdeka Tournament">Merdeka Tournament</a>. However, Malaysia lost on penalties to Vietnam. Sathianathan also led Malaysia to the semi finals of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Myanmar_Grand_Royal_Challenge_Cup" title="2008 Myanmar Grand Royal Challenge Cup">2008 Myanmar Grand Royal Challenge Cup</a>. However, Malaysia then shockingly lost 4–1 to eventual winners, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_national_football_team" title="Myanmar national football team">Myanmar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2008_AFF_Championship" title="2008 AFF Championship">2008 AFF Championship</a>, Malaysia started their campaign with a 3–0 win over Laos, but were defeated in the second match by Vietnam with a score of 2–3 and were finally eliminated when they lost 3–0 to Thailand in the final match of the group stage. This was the first time that the Malaysian squad had not passed through the group stages in 12 years.</p>
<p>In the 2011 Asian Cup qualifiers, the Malaysian team lost 0–5 to the United Arab Emirates. This defeat was the final straw in the eyes of Malaysian supporters, and in February 2009, the contracts of Sathianathan and manager <a href="/wiki/Soh_Chin_Aun" title="Soh Chin Aun">Soh Chin Aun</a> were terminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Harimau_Muda_A" title="Harimau Muda A">U-20 Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Selangor_FA" title="Selangor FA">Selangor FA</a> coach, <a href="/wiki/Malay_styles_and_titles" title="Malay styles and titles">Datuk</a> <a href="/wiki/K._Rajagopal" title="K. Rajagopal">K. Rajagopal</a> was selected as the new head coach for Malaysia. He took over in July 2009.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_AFF_Championship_triumph">2010 AFF Championship triumph</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010 AFF Championship triumph">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="534" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg/220px-IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg/330px-IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg/440px-IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IDN-MAS_2010-12-29.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship" title="2010 AFF Championship">2010 AFF Championship</a> winners <b>(blue)</b>, <a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship#Final" title="2010 AFF Championship">second leg of final</a> starting line-up.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In April 2009, <a href="/wiki/Malay_styles_and_titles" title="Malay styles and titles">Datuk</a> <a href="/wiki/K._Rajagopal" title="K. Rajagopal">K. Rajagopal</a> was named the new coach of Malaysia replacing <a href="/wiki/B._Sathianathan" title="B. Sathianathan">B. Sathianathan</a> as head coach of Malaysia. K. Rajagopal was also the coach of the Malaysia Under-23 squad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> K. Rajagopal's first match was against <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_football_team" title="Zimbabwe national football team">Zimbabwe</a>, which Malaysia won 4–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> Rajagopal also coached Malaysia in two games against visiting English champions, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, losing both matches 2–3 and 0–2. During his time as the coach of the Under-23 team, K. Rajagopal led Malaysia to their fifth <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2009_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Football at the 2009 Southeast Asian Games">SEA Games</a> gold medal and also led Malaysia to qualify for the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Games" title="2010 Asian Games">2010 Asian Games</a> as one of the best four third-placed teams after a lapse of 32 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship" title="2010 AFF Championship">2010 AFF Championship</a>, Malaysia had 14 players that were under the age of 23 while the other players were over 23. Malaysia were in group A with host <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_national_football_team" title="Indonesia national football team">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand</a> and qualifiers winner, <a href="/wiki/Laos_national_football_team" title="Laos national football team">Laos</a>. Malaysia began their campaign with an embarrassing 5–1 loss to Indonesia. Malaysia bounced back from their defeat and later drew with Thailand and beat Laos 5–1. As runner up of group, Malaysia qualified for the semi finals to meet Group B winners and defending champions <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_national_football_team" title="Vietnam national football team">Vietnam</a>. In the first leg of the semifinal, Malaysia won 2–0 on home soil and later drew 0–0 in the second leg, advancing to the final with an aggregate of 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In the finals, Malaysia met favourites Indonesia, who were unbeaten in all their matches.</p>
<p>On the first leg of the finals, Malaysia won 3–0 at home. Malaysia scored twice through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohd_Safee_Mohd_Sali" title="Mohd Safee Mohd Sali">Safee Sali</a> and once through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohd_Ashaari_Shamsuddin" title="Mohd Ashaari Shamsuddin">Mohd Ashaari Shamsuddin</a> on a night when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Bukit_Jalil" title="National Stadium, Bukit Jalil">Bukit Jalil National Stadium</a> was filled over capacity for the first time since it was built. The match attracted so many people that after tickets were sold out, policemen manning the gates were seen allowing friends and relatives into the stadium, causing people having to trespass onto the cable bridge above the electronic display besides standing on the aisles and corridors to view the game. On the second leg of the finals that was held in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Malaysia lost 2–1 to Indonesia but the final aggregate was 4–2 to Malaysia, thus Malaysia were awarded the title. It was the first time in history that Malaysia were crowned the champions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> (AFF Championship Champions) and a trophy in the international stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit">Kit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the 1970s to 2007, the national team kit was manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, who also sponsored the national team kit. Since 2007, the official Malaysia team kit has been manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>. The home kit's design of black and yellow stripes is a throwback to the kit used by Malaysian national team of the 1920s. The great national team of the 1970s also sported similar stripes, which are supposed to be reminiscent of the stripes of a tiger, the symbol of Malaysia's national football team.</p>
<p>In November 2010, Nike Malaysia created a new football kit for the Malaysians specially made for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Suzuki_Cup" title="2010 AFF Suzuki Cup">2010 AFF Suzuki Cup</a>. The home kit's design of black and yellow stripes is shaped by a black row of lines. The away kit features a plain blue front and red and white at the edge of the sleeves. Nike used the Malaysian flag as their logo instead of putting the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">Football Association of Malaysia</a> logo to remembering the team success in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> On the underside of the flag, the quote "<i>Tanah Tumpahnya Darahku</i>" (The land that I spill my blood for) can be found. The quote is part of the <a href="/wiki/Negaraku" title="Negaraku">Malaysia National Anthem</a>, alluding that they are doing their best for the country.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training">Training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisma_FAM" title="Wisma FAM">Wisma FAM</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wisma_FAM" title="Wisma FAM">Wisma FAM</a> is a training facility and the main headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">Football Association of Malaysia</a> which located at <a href="/wiki/Kelana_Jaya" title="Kelana Jaya">Kelana Jaya</a>, Malaysia. The facility is founded by the association with a purpose to serve as a headquarters and also as a training ground for the national team. Others than that, it serves as a meeting point, a room for press statement and small apartment rooms available for the national players. Sometimes, ticket matches also sold on this training facility.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Malaysia home matches and some away matches (depending on the location and the broadcast station) are shown live or delayed on <a href="/wiki/Astro_Arena_(TV_channel)" title="Astro Arena (TV channel)">Astro Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Televisyen_Malaysia" title="Radio Televisyen Malaysia">RTM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_Prima" title="Media Prima">Media Prima</a>. All matches are broadcast with in full <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_language" title="Malaysian language">Malaysian commentary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsors">Sponsors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sponsors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the website of <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Malaysia" title="Football Association of Malaysia">Football Association of Malaysia</a>, Malaysia main sponsors include <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_Islam" title="Bank Islam">Bank Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/100plus" title="100plus">100plus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telekom_Malaysia" title="Telekom Malaysia">Telekom Malaysia</a> and One Goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_stadium">Home stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Home stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg/220px-National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg/330px-National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg/440px-National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bukit_Jalil_National_Stadium" title="Bukit Jalil National Stadium">Bukit Jalil National Stadium</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Malaysia's home stadium is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Bukit_Jalil" title="National Stadium, Bukit Jalil">Bukit Jalil National Stadium</a>. The stadium capacity is 87,411 (seated)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> which makes it the third <a href="/wiki/List_of_association_football_stadiums_by_capacity" title="List of association football stadiums by capacity">largest football stadium in the world</a>. Malaysia's previous national stadium was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merdeka_Stadium" title="Merdeka Stadium">Merdeka Stadium</a> before the Bukit Jalil sports complex was constructed. Malaysia also uses other stadiums for their matches such as the <a href="/wiki/KLFA_Stadium" title="KLFA Stadium">KLFA Stadium</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBPJ_Stadium" title="MBPJ Stadium">MBPJ Stadium</a> , the <a href="/wiki/Shah_Alam_Stadium" title="Shah Alam Stadium">Shah Alam Stadium</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Larkin_Stadium" title="Larkin Stadium">Larkin Stadium</a> .</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Ultras Malaya</b> is the name of the major supporters for the national team in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. They are known for their high fanaticism and support towards the national team. Even in every international match the national team played, they will be found in a group standing at the supporters area. The main colours for these supporter are usually in black with a yellow <a href="/wiki/Scarf" title="Scarf">scarf</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banners" title="Banners">banners</a> just like the national team kits colours. These supporters always bring <a href="/wiki/Flare#Flares_and_football" title="Flare">flares</a>, drums and large national flags to the stadiums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_record">Competitive record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Competitive record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FIFA_.27A.27_international_matches">FIFA 'A' international matches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: FIFA 'A' international matches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia"><img alt="Malaysia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Ong_Kim_Swee" title="Ong Kim Swee">Ong Kim Swee</a> (2014<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_7"><a href="#endnote_7">2</a></sup>, 2015–)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>1.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_6"><b><a href="#ref_6">^</a></b></span> Earned Malaysian nationality after Malaysia formed on 16 September 1963. Became Singaporean after <a href="/wiki/Singapore_in_Malaysia" title="Singapore in Malaysia">Singapore separation from Malaysia</a> in 1965.<br/>
2.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_7"><b><a href="#ref_7">^</a></b></span>  – managed the team on a one-off basis as <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_manager" title="Caretaker manager">caretaker manager</a>.</p>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 December</span> 2014</span>. <q>Rubbing salt to injury when Malaysia lost to Singapore, the national media and football pundits avoided using Harimau Malaya when referring to the national team preferring to refer the team as Malaysia. Perhaps they thought it was allright to include Sarawak and Sabah when the going got rough. But when Malaysia beat Indonesia last Saturday night, the national newspapers went to town with the triumph of Harimau Malaya – when the going is good it seems there is no room for the East Malaysian states.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMalaysia+national+football+team&amp;rft.au=Peter+Sibon&amp;rft.btitle=Harimau+Malaya+%93+where+is+East+M%27sia+in+the+national+team%3F&amp;rft.date=2012-12-06&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.theborneopost.com%2F2012%2F12%2F06%2Fharimau-malaya-where-is-east-msia-in-the-national-team%2F&amp;rft.pub=The+Borneo+Post&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
